< Review>
Met up with a cousin for breakfast. It was nice and quite so we felt we'd have no problem get hot fresh food. The friendly counter attendant took our order from their menu and confirmed the toppings that came on our order. (5 stars for friendly service), our meal finally arrived well over 20 to 25 minutes later. There were only 3 other people having breakfast and no one else. We ordered the most simplest Mexican dish ever made Chilaqiles plate with rice and beans. Most but not all Mexican restaurant opt to use canned refried beans which was evident in the taste. Rice was average like everyone else's. However the biggest let down was the main course of Chilaqiles which had minimal amount of cheese... Which many other places offer  authentic Queso Fresco which is crumbled over the meal. It taste way better and the tortilla chips were completely bland and soggy. 90% of Mexican restaurants prepare this dish in a way that the chips have a crispness to the chips the sause is not over drenched. The additional topping of chopped onion is added to give flavor to the meal. (Optional by the way if you like onion.) I personally have made Chilaqiles at home countless times for family and friends. Even going so far as to use pre-fried chips from the Mexican supermarkets to expidite not having to fry a large amount chips on the fly. But to have to wait over 20 min for microwaved food is unacceptable. I didnt read the reviews before inviting my guest and even he spoke up and mentioned he wasn't impressed with the taste, and quality of the meal for the price and especially for the wait. I can't give an opinion on the rest of their menu to be honest. However if in the simplest of meals ever to come out of a Mexican kitchen which quite literally cost next to nothing to make, you don't hit it out of the ballpark... That speaks volumes of what I can expect from the rest of the menu offerings.</Review>

1. My car was towed from the very parking lot I was told was okay to park in while charging my car because, as you'll see from the pictures below, the chargers are ALWAYS broken. I was told I could charge my car in a designated area as long as I moved it before 7 a.m. (at some point it was 8 a.m., but they keep changing the rules without any notice). The tow slip says they came at 4 a.m. The parking lot was completely empty (not in anyone's way) and wasn't notified or given a chance to move it (I live here; they have my phone and unit number). More than $500 down the drain! One receptionist said their staff usually never do do something like this, and that I should reach out to their managers. I did - multiple times - and not a single reply back from anyone.
2. The pool has been unusable for almost half a year, and doesn't seem to be fixed any time soon. Just a few stagnant, dirty inches of water in the pool and the jacuzzi.
3. Elevators are down on an occasional basis. At one point, all three of the elevators closest to our unit were down for days.
4. Fire alarms are extremely sensitive and go off at all times of the day, but especially at night when one is trying to sleep.
5. Demolishments in the metro yard right next door is aggressive, with every concrete wall that falls making it feel like the a 5.0 earthquake throughout the day.
6. My car was parked in the gated resident parking right under a security camera and was broken into (their gates also break constantly and are left open so anyone can go in and out). I requested to view the footage so I can complete my police report and they wouldn't let me view it or have a copy.
7. In general, they will lie, or provide false statements, as to what services they offer and what the guidelines are. Then, will arbitrarily change them and you may incur additional fees because of if. Like they way they decided to change the way they receive and disperse packages.

I cannot stress enough the headaches this building has put us through. Be skeptical of the 5-star ratings; reception has a sign asking for them. The only reason this place gets the one star is for *some* of their friendly reception and handy-worker staff.<//review>

<text>There is a reason why so many people have left 1 star reviews for this apartment building. While the building itself is modern and in a nice area of the Arts District,  and the concierge staff are really great, the management is frustratingly bad. There are very high monthly fees - you get charged a mandatory $25/month for a trash pickup service to your door (even though there's trash chutes along the corridor), $20 for sewer, and $100 or more per month for electricity and water usage fees (water is split evenly between all apartments and always high, nothing can be done about it).

SECURITY DEPOSIT - Mandatory fees will be removed from your deposit
We left the apartment as clean as we found it moving in, but they remove what they call 'standard fees' from the security deposit, which includes a $165 cleaning fee, and $250 wall painting fee! After a lot of complaining they finally removed the cleaning fee but are still charging us a pro-rated wall painting fee (we lived there for 13 months, didn't paint or damage the walls, and filled in all picture hanging holes and repainted them with the correct color paint, but apparently that's still not enough). This is the first place I've lived in my life that I won't get my deposit back fully. We plan to fight it as it doesn't seem legal.

FRUSTRATING PRACTICES - charged $400 for parking in wrong spot in my apartment building (rather than a simple phone call to move).
Berkshire Communities employs a lot of temp workers so when we moved in they couldn't help with quite a few questions. When we moved into the apartment, the temp pointed out some parking spaces with large white signs that were for the Metro parking *but* didn't say that most of the 2nd floor parking is Metro only (with small floor-painted writing half-faded, much less obvious than the few large white signs). Within the first couple of weeks I accidentally parked in a spot one night and came down the next morning to find my car towed. I had to pay $400 to get the car back. Note I had a One Santa Fe resident parking sticker visible on my window screen. I parked the car at ~8pm and came down at 630am to find the car towed overnight. When I picked up the car, it had a big sticker on the driver's side of the windscreen that took me a lot of elbow grease to completely remove. All they needed to do was call me and I would have moved it immediately. The parking in building 100 is never full so this really was unnecessary. I contacted management about it but they just said there was nothing to be done. I asked them to please paint the faded floor writing for other residents, but they never did.

BUILDING LAYOUT
There is no access to stairwells except to exit, so when the elevators break (once our elevator was broken for 3 weeks) you have to walk to the other end of the building to use a different elevator as stairs are inaccessible. There is no way to access the gym/pool except by elevator, so again, when it broke, I had to walk the entirety of the building to go through another entrance area. If you live in the 100 building there is no access to the courtyard, so you have to exit the building to the street and re-enter through the drive-in entrance.

COMMUNITY FORUM shutdown
There used to be a residents online forum to chat, but when people noticed the high monthly fees being charged, and started talking about it on the forum, management shut it down! Luckily we saw this and spoke to management and they did reduce our monthly fees after that (apparently there was an 'error' in their overcharging us!).

HOT TUBS
Are excellent, generally very hot, with a great view of the city.<//text>< pics>
None</pics>

UPDATE: so the main selling points of this apartment complex were the amenities and location for me...with that, the location is still great, but I've lived here for 9 months and of the 9 months, 7 of them I have been unable to use the pool that they boasted about upon showing their space. There have been numerous emails saying they're fixing it, then later stating that they will connect us with a local pool for us to use...there has been no deliverance of said claims however. I've reached out to the desk multiple times about this and now have called the property manager so I'm waiting to hear back, but for the amount of money everyone here pays on rent for and this to continue without any claims being fulfilled, I think residents should get a bit of reimbursement.

The elevators are also intermittently breaking and I can only imagine any person requiring one being stuck :/. As for me, it's been a pretty sizable inconvenience every time it happens, since I've been needing to transport large equipment.

I also am unsure of how safe/secure this building is, as a few nights ago at 5:30 am, someone tried to enter my apartment. I went to the office to inquire what that was about, and if they had changed the keys before I moved in, how many copies there were, etc. The desk did not seem worried about any of this, and simply made a note and told me to call them next time it happens. I was also told to not bother calling the cops. I honestly don't know what to make of this and have been since barricading my door each night as I sleep to better take my safety into my own hands.

I would also like to mention that all the appliances used in this building are subpar at best, or at least in my unit. <userid>103741301531365324072< /userid>< Name>
Alex Phi</Name>
<date>1493697384815</date><rate>2<//rate>< review>
Big "A" Architecture with Big "O" Overrrated.

As a member of the architecture community, in all seriousness, I must review this one with no sarcasm nor wittiness yet with the same enthusiasm as the rest of my reviews.  This review will not critique the staff in which were stellar the day they gave employees of the architecture firm I work for (Gensler) an exclusive private open house which included tours, wine, and after party.

Typical Michael Maltzan building.  Designed as an white object only understood by seeing it from a mile in the sky.  Designed too big for its own good.  Someone with a lot of cash living somewhere far away decided to cram the most units they could into one thin strip and maximize their value.  Besides it's long linear form, it completely ignores and dwarfs everything around it (that's what she said! Okay that's my only one).

Lack of Human Scale

This portion is for you, the reader, the potential renter, the guy going for drinks at the restaurant below, the girl going to shop at the boutique store.  The complex may look great flying by at 60 mph but once you get out of the car and walk along the building, it lacks the single attribute a pedestrian would want in an experience.  That's human scale.

The amazing lifestyle that the renderings portrayed just doesn't exist because it just wasn't designed at that scale.  The bare and cold facades along with the lack of landscaping makes it a unbearable to walk along.  The same goes with all of the massive parking garages and eerie long hallways of the complex.

My last critique is on the little detail or lets call it ornamentation on the building, the window brise soleil.  It's obviously ornamentation for the building, because it shows up only on some windows yet not others.  The side of the building that I would say needs it most is the west facade yet they only show up on the east facade.  Some slightly north facing facades have them even though the sun never hits the window.  Sun studies people! Architecture 101.

Sorry Michael, this one was a flop, although I'm waiting for restaurants and shops to move in to see if life gets better on the ground floor.  Updates to come.< /review>

< review>
As much as I want to support the local businesses, I highly do NOT recommend doing business that lacks integrity and blames their customers. I resorted to filing a complaint with the California Board of Optometry (Board) for the reason below.

I‚Äôve visited this optometry in the past to get an eye exam (contact and lens) and to order new contact and spectacle lens using insurance. The eye exams provided by the licensed optometrists have been great without any issues. But the latest experience was questionable and distasteful in regards to their business practice.

The optometrist had completed the eye exam and afterward, the staff (optician?) guided me to another room to conduct the optomap exam ($49 not covered by insurance). Never did the optician informed me that there is an extra cost to this extra service. Afterward, had a consultation with another optician to replace the lens on existing glasses, and it went downhill from here. I‚Äôve asked if it‚Äôs possible to get my pair of backup glasses cleaned and shown him the lens that had spray paints on it. Keep in mind the lens is not smeared in white paint but the overspray getting to the lens, tiny dots of white paint. The optician said he will try and came back with what appeared to have rendered the lens useless, ruining the top coat with smears. Mind you there were no smears on the top coating at all. The optometrist refused to fix this issue and the optician blamed the aging and wear and tear. If the optician was experienced and helps patients daily cleaning their glasses, he should have known better and advised the patient that they are not able to remove it rather than ruining the lens.

I had to visit the optometrist the second to bring up this issue with the manager, but they said they will only offer a special discount (which I‚Äôve never received), and the owner, Dr. Ahn didn‚Äôt even bother acknowledging me during this visit when I was the only customer during the Covid19 lockdown. The first visit, which was unnecessary and a waste of my time, was because the optician forgot to add the transition/photochromic order to the spectacle lens so I had to drive to the store for them to correct their mistake.

After filing a formal complaint with the Board did Dr. Ahn emailed me to offer the free replacement of the backup glasses. The complaint against Dr. Esther Ahn Optometry was for several reasons but I‚Äôll only point to one violation here. The optometry has been incorrectly issuing spectacle lens prescriptions for only one year rather than two years as required by the California Business and Professions Code ¬ß2541.1(b). The optometry responded to the Board that their software vendor had set the default setting to one year. In my opinion, the optometry was negligent by not verifying and changing the software setting. This only means the optometry has been prescribing incorrect spectacle lens prescriptions to hundreds and thousands of patients for however many years.

Please check your prescriptions and if this optometry had prescribed you for only one year recently, file a complaint with the Board.< /review>

<Time>1583164734787</Time><userid>100628241609761386745</userid><Rate>5< /Rate><GmapID>0x80c2c35140969c8b:0xe43bb826e48c7cf8</GmapID><Text>SINGAPORE üá∏üá¨
Excerpt from Eat the World Los Angeles:
If you have ever traveled in Singapore and some of the larger cities of Malaysia and Indonesia, the letter Q used twice in names will be very familiar. Small street vendors, hawker stalls, and full restaurants all use it similarly, most of which have nothing to do with each other. The term originated in Taiwan and has spread throughout the Chinese-speaking world with many meanings and usages.

In terms of food, the literal translation is akin to "chewy," the Taiwanese version of which sounds like the way people say the letter Q in English. Chewy does not tell the whole story of QQ though, as it implies that the item in question has a good resistance and mouthfeel. Not too soft, a good bounce, nice and chewy.

A good introduction and a wonderful barometer of how satisfying the QQ here will be is a handsome plate of Singapore char kway teow ($9.95). Also full of the other textures from meats, vegetables, and egg, the broad flat noodles have some of the best QQ in town and are the perfect vehicle for a well-balanced blend of seasoning and good spice level. Each bite of the char kway teow reveals a deep level of skill by the chef and just the right amount of each ingredient. When the meats (beef, Taiwanese sausage, shrimp) and vegetables are slightly charred, they give the surrounding elements even more flavor, a technique Cantonese chefs describe as "wok hei" or "wok's breath" in English. This simple phrase might be the best way to describe the simple satisfaction that comes from eating the dish.<//Text><user_name>Jared Cohee<//user_name><pics>[{'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipNAy_zZU6bOjTEcpjmcAd7KdD0dJYFy6R4U_OFL=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipPe4_gxTkHZiW2bsIImlC_Tbk0zvHStO8n5pYAn=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipMdzPAq4SPQbNcdMEPz3KuBGf56yvuOR8-3tSnK=w150-h150-k-no-p']}]< /pics>< Response>

< Review>
Small fast food outpost serving inexpensive Asian dishes. Most items on the menu are good, not great. Laksa is the curry style rather than the assam style. The test of any Hainanese chicken rice dish is the rice and the one here is not fragrant at all. Still, if you're looking for Indonesian, Singaporean or Malaysian food in a pinch, this place would serve you well.< /Review>

<name>Robert Gilbert< /name><Date>1552172178133</Date><Rating>4< /Rating>< Review>
The picture displays of each of item is a blessing and a curse. On one end it makes your mouth water. On the other hand you get your sandwich and it does not look the same.
My time going in I was behind 1 other with a slightly larger order. One staff member made nearly the entire order as well as ours while the others stood around the wait was quite lengthy.
This is just a nitpick but the walls are very bare. Hopefully in time they can build a nice modern look to drawn in customers to stay longer.

The real test here of course is the food. The price is a little unbelievable. For what could get you 2 "foot longs" at competitive sandwich places (around 11 dollars). Besides that, I ordered the Fonz triple star. The flavors. The flavors explode and hit all the right places. This spot could be the place to be if it just felt more inviting and quicker paced... And if the price didn't seem so steep.

All in all the sandwich has me wanting those flavors but seeing the simple ingredients I don't know if Id want to pay that price from something I can grab from my local grocery store .</Review>
